<p>The name of our class is now <strong>Person. </strong>When working with a class, the name should have the following characteristics:</p></code></code></pre><pre class="vditor-wysiwyg__preview" data-render="1"><div data-block-id="396f12f0c37021650a4976f6bc5536e4" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 953.963px; left: 6.037px; top: 451px;" data-block-type="text" class="sl-block"><div style="z-index: 13;" data-placeholder-text="Text" data-placeholder-tag="p" class="sl-block-content" data-gramm_id="8c5b532f-d42d-4681-eaea-a1b5a933039a" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true"><code>
<p>The name of our class is now <strong>Person. </strong>When working with a class, the name should have the following characteristics:</p></code></div></div></pre></div><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code><code><ul>
	<li>Be a noun</li>

<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" data-block-id="553b1ef6a2e5a4cf1ccd53e11af3fbbe" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 960px; left: 0px; top: 336px;"><div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 14;" data-gramm_id="3bcd7ec4-2887-40d1-3e89-eabeaa161e19" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true">

</div></section><section data-id="c2d8c46427dea8afc29ec6debb226f30">
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" data-block-id="a68ef6151ee4e4491f34995a3413dda5" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 800px; left: 80px; top: 66.5px;"><div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 10;" data-gramm_id="5e6c072e-8c3b-ae89-3c4c-01896fd36cd1" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true">
<p style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);"><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17); text-align: justify;">Think of a class as a template that we use to create individual objects. </span><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);">It is a set of instructions that describe how an object should behave. Every Java class is made up of the following parts: </span></p></code></code></pre><pre class="vditor-wysiwyg__preview" data-render="1"><ul><code>
	<li data-node-id="20221202101316-p8qxnl3"><p>Be a noun</p></li>
	<li data-node-id="20221202101316-v1dmg2t"><p>The first letter of each new word should be capitalized.Â </p></li>
</code></ul><code>
</code></pre></div></div><code>
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" data-block-id="553b1ef6a2e5a4cf1ccd53e11af3fbbe" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 960px; left: 0px; top: 336px;"><div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 14;" data-gramm_id="3bcd7ec4-2887-40d1-3e89-eabeaa161e19" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true">
<p>Every time you have been selecting New -> Class, you have been creating a new class. We haven't been treating it as a class but that is what has been happening.Â </p>
</div></div>
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" style="width: 960px; left: 0px; top: 0px; height: auto;" data-name="text-1d2448" data-block-id="81ee9a48c36532b3fa8eea418e3307de">
<div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="h1" data-placeholder-text="Title Text" style="z-index: 15;" dir="ui">
<h2>Java OOP Day 2</h2>

<grammarly-extension style="position: absolute; top: 0px; left: 0px; pointer-events: none; z-index: 10;" class="_1KJtL"></grammarly-extension>

<section data-id="c2d8c46427dea8afc29ec6debb226f30"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code>
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" data-block-id="a68ef6151ee4e4491f34995a3413dda5" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 800px; left: 80px; top: 66.5px;"><div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 10;" data-gramm_id="5e6c072e-8c3b-ae89-3c4c-01896fd36cd1" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true">
<p style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);"><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17); text-align: justify;">Think of a class as a template that we use to create individual objects. </span><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);">It is a set of instructions that describe how an object should behave. Every Java class is made up of the following parts: </span></p></div><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code><ul>
	<li style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);">
<strong>Instance Variables</strong></code></pre><pre class="vditor-wysiwyg__preview" data-render="1"><ul><li style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);"><p>
<strong>Instance Variables</strong></p></li></ul></pre></div><p data-block="0">	<code data-type="html-inline"><ul></code>
		<code data-type="html-inline"><li style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);"></code><code data-type="html-inline"><span style="text-align: justify;"></code>Instance variables are variables within a class but outside any method<code data-type="html-inline"></li></code>
	<code data-type="html-inline"></ul></code>
	<code data-type="html-inline"></li></code>
	<code data-type="html-inline"><li style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);"></code>
<code data-type="html-inline"><strong></code><code data-type="html-inline"><span style="text-align: justify;"></code>Constructors<code data-type="html-inline"></strong></code>
	<code data-type="html-inline"><ul></code>
		<code data-type="html-inline"><li style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);"></code><code data-type="html-inline"><span style="text-align: justify;"></code>Allows instances of our classes to be created<span class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-entity"><code data-type="html-entity" style="display:none">&nbsp;</code><span class="vditor-wysiwyg__preview" data-render="2"><code>Â </code></span></span> <span class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-entity"><code data-type="html-entity" style="display:none">&nbsp;</code><span class="vditor-wysiwyg__preview" data-render="2"><code>Â </code></span></span><code data-type="html-inline"></li></code>
		<code data-type="html-inline"><li style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17); text-align: justify;"></code>They set up the specifications for each instance<code data-type="html-inline"></li></code>
	<code data-type="html-inline"></ul></code>
	<code data-type="html-inline"></li></code>
	<code data-type="html-inline"><li style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17); text-align: left;"></code>
<code data-type="html-inline"><strong></code>Methods<code data-type="html-inline"></strong></code>
	<code data-type="html-inline"><ul></code>
		<code data-type="html-inline"><li style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17); text-align: left;"></code>describes the kind of functionality and behavior of the class.<code data-type="html-inline"></li></code>
	<code data-type="html-inline"></ul></code>
	<code data-type="html-inline"></li></code></p><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code></ul>
</div></div>
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" style="width: 960px; left: 0px; top: 0px; height: auto;" data-name="text-1d2448" data-block-id="016b1a60c7d5f350f16c408e891e732e">
<div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="h1" data-placeholder-text="Title Text" style="z-index: 11;" dir="ui">
<h2>Java OOP Day 2</h2>
</div>
<grammarly-extension style="position: absolute; top: 0px; left: 0px; pointer-events: none; z-index: 10;" class="_1KJtL"></grammarly-extension>
</div></section><section data-id="d1b45f4dcc7045029053b9b246c26912">
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" style="height: auto; width: 800px; left: 80px; top: 84px;" data-block-id="85355a6f546ce78e70e19c53f4107779"><div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 10;" data-gramm_id="5e6c072e-8c3b-ae89-3c4c-01896fd36cd1" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true" dir="ui">
<p style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);"><strong>Access Modifiers</strong></p>
<p style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);">Variables and methods have different <em>access modifiers</em>&nbsp;that can be used.</p>
<ul>
<li style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);">
<strong>Default</strong>: without an access modifier specified, they are accessible only within the same package</li>
<li style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);">
<strong>Private: </strong>can only be accessed within the class it is declared</li>
<li style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);">
<strong>Protected:</strong>&nbsp;accessible within the same package or sub classes in different packages</li>
<li style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);">
<strong>Public</strong>:<strong>&nbsp;</strong>can be accessed from every where in the program</li>
</ul>
</div></div>
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" style="width: 960px; left: 0px; top: 0px; height: auto;" data-name="text-1d2448" data-block-id="be08aeb176d584720a3234299424a46b">
<div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="h1" data-placeholder-text="Title Text" style="z-index: 11;" dir="ui">
<h2>Java OOP Day 2</h2>
</div>
<grammarly-extension style="position: absolute; top: 0px; left: 0px; pointer-events: none; z-index: 10;" class="_1KJtL"></grammarly-extension>
</div></section><section data-id="54ffc1abe4d9c0f4b8dd703516a81e11">
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" data-block-id="64abfbee87a07300a714052383fa787f" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 512px; left: 32px; top: 149px;"><div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 10;" data-gramm_id="f048609a-37f4-c4da-f551-3488f713b9f1" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true">
<ul>
	<li>Instance Variables are associated with objects</li>
	<li>They get created inside of a class but outside of what is known as a method.</li>
	<li>They're free floaters</li>
	<li>They get initialized (/defined) when an instance of our class is created</li>
	<li>Each instance of our class may have unique values for each instance variable</li>
</ul>
</div></div>
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="image" data-block-id="70a76f0db172cc1c5590244ed41c8165" style="min-width: 1px; min-height: 1px; width: 355px; height: 355px; left: 569px; top: 173px;"><div class="sl-block-content" style="z-index: 11;"><img data-natural-width="160" data-natural-height="160" style="" data-lazy-loaded="" data-src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/media-p.slid.es/uploads/264630/images/5621934/giphy.gif"></div></div>

<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" data-name="text-9487d3" data-block-id="23112bca46535f260baad383c08cc9f4" style="height: auto; width: 600px; left: 180px; top: 89.8123px;"><div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 14;">
<p><strong>Instance Variables</strong></p>
</div></div></section><section data-id="37d1fee2100abc5c81704f196840d77a">
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" style="height: auto; width: 800px; left: 80px; top: 110px;" data-block-id="19836c2c552f5938328d7b283ca35d72"><div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 10;" data-gramm_id="f048609a-37f4-c4da-f551-3488f713b9f1" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true">
<ul>
	<li>Instance Variables are dependent on the instance of our class</li>
	<li>You can make instance variables private, public, protected
	<ul>
		<li>Private variables are often called properties</li>
	</ul>
	</li>
	<li>Can use any of the four access levels (which means they can be marked with any of the three access modifiers)</li>
	<li>Cannot be marked static, because then they'd become class variables.</li>
</ul>
</div></div>

<section data-id="f78ed3da1a671b5ccbb8350a8a92ac48"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code>
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="code" data-block-id="c3c9c3836392b8879b81a775fd0a780a" style="min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 387px; height: 221px; left: 298px; top: 190px;"><div class="sl-block-content notranslate" data-highlight-theme="monokai-sublime" style="z-index: 10; font-size: 169%;"><pre class="java"><code>public class Person{</code></pre></div><p data-block="0"><code>    String name;
    int age;
    String location;
}
<code data-type="html-inline"></code></code><code data-type="html-inline"></pre></code><code data-type="html-inline"></div></code><code data-type="html-inline"></div></code></code></p><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code><code><div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" data-block-id="4dcd7438f793346d577d3ccd2aa3865f" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 600px; left: 180px; top: 440px;"><div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 11;" data-gramm_id="7cb61a5a-6c58-4e98-0e82-a21324937c04" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true">
<p>We now have three instance variables (<strong>name, age, and location). </strong> They have no value yet but they do exist, they're just empty at the moment.&nbsp;</p>

<section data-id="902bf783a6aadb2acd3db1a398a42fe5"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code><code>

<p>You can have as many constructors as you wish. However, the more constructors you have the higher the possibility that your instances are incredibly different from one another.</p></div><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code><p>&nbsp;</p></code></pre><pre class="vditor-wysiwyg__preview" data-render="1"><p>Â </p></pre></div><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code><p><strong>Empty</strong><strong>&nbsp;Constructor</strong></p></code></pre><pre class="vditor-wysiwyg__preview" data-render="1"><p><strong>Empty</strong><strong>Â Constructor</strong></p></pre></div><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code><p><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);">You can also have an empty constructor. <p style="text-align: left;">When creating an object:</p></code></code></code></code></pre><pre class="vditor-wysiwyg__preview" data-render="1"><div data-block-id="5b95c107b5b94f68e9873d5c215ba944" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 855px; left: 51px; top: 247px;" data-block-type="text" class="sl-block"><div style="z-index: 10;" data-placeholder-text="Text" data-placeholder-tag="p" class="sl-block-content" data-gramm_id="6000c23d-51b4-4bf8-3873-4f1e295f7aec" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code><code>
<p style="text-align: left;">When creating an object:</p></code></code></code></div></div></pre></div><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code><code><code><ul>
	<li style="text-align: left;">We call the class we want to create the object from and associate it with a variable name.</li>
	<li style="text-align: left;">We use the 'new' keyword to create the object (an instance of our class), allowing it to inherit the characteristics of our Person class (all variables and methods).</li>
	<li style="text-align: left;">After "new" is the constructor we want to use to construct our new object. This constructor initializes the new object.</li>
</ul>
</div></div>
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="code" style="width: 567px; height: 54px; left: 190px; top: 171px;" data-block-id="1d70fee1cef6771c589abca5a21763a6"><div class="sl-block-content notranslate" data-highlight-theme="monokai-sublime" style="z-index: 11; font-size: 133%;"><pre class="java"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;">Person secondPerson = new Person("John");</code></pre></div></div>
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="code" style="min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 467px; height: 54px; left: 240px; top: 101px;" data-block-id="4648a1294eb960cd0e4e37ecf1e46379"><div class="sl-block-content notranslate" data-highlight-theme="monokai-sublime" style="z-index: 12; font-size: 133%;"><pre class="java"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;">Person firstPerson = new Person();</code></pre></div></div>

<section data-id="04d92577a5dc3c7f0751a2a3064ad5db"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code>
<div style="width: 617px; height: 368px; left: 171px; top: 192px;" data-block-type="code" class="sl-block" data-block-id="a7fb043409c68b9a6f9d0615f0b731ae"><div style="z-index: 10; border-top-style: solid; border-right-style: solid; border-bottom-style: solid; border-left-style: solid; border-top-width: 1px; border-right-width: 1px; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-left-width: 1px; border-top-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-right-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-bottom-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-left-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-top-left-radius: 5px; border-top-right-radius: 5px; border-bottom-right-radius: 5px; border-bottom-left-radius: 5px;" class="sl-block-content notranslate" data-highlight-theme="monokai-sublime"><pre class="java"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;">import java.io.Console;
import java.util.*;</code></pre></div><p data-block="0"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;">public class Person{
   // variables and constructor</code></p><p data-block="0"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;">   public void sayHello(){
   	System.out.println("Hello, my name is " +  name);
   }</code></p><p data-block="0"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;">   public static void main(String[] args){
       Person firstPerson = new Person();
       Person secondPerson = new Person("John");
       Person thirdPerson = new Person("Jane", 45, "London");</code></p><p data-block="0"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;">        thirdPerson.sayHello();
   }
}</code></p><p data-block="0"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;">    <code data-type="html-inline"></code></code><code data-type="html-inline"></pre></code><code data-type="html-inline"></div></code><code data-type="html-inline"></div></code></code></p><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code><div style="height: auto; width: 935px; left: 13px; top: 70px;" data-block-type="text" class="sl-block" data-block-id="b419ba6b1dcc7d842a4595b8292ea33f"><div style="z-index: 11;" data-placeholder-text="Text" data-placeholder-tag="p" class="sl-block-content" data-gramm_id="20db7505-3458-d317-9382-2a7e13a5d703" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true">
<p>To get to the codes that our method contains we need to call it.&nbsp; To call a class method, you must use the format "<span style="color: rgb(0, 128, 0);">ObjectName.Method()</span><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0);">".&nbsp; In the example below, we call the method with </span><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);">thirdPerson.sayHello();</span></p>
</div></div>
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="code" style="width: 253px; height: 62px; left: 240px; top: 568px;" data-block-id="568eefd7ef14a1340e4fdd520a28fd07"><div class="sl-block-content notranslate" data-highlight-theme="zenburn" style="z-index: 12; font-size: 225%;"><pre class="java"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;">Hello Jane
</code></pre></div></div>

<p><span style="text-align: center;">A </span><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);"><span style="text-align: center;">method</span></span><span style="text-align: center;"> can do more than just print to screen its results.</span></p>

<p style="color: rgb(255, 255, 255); text-align: center;"><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0);">The command </span><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);"><span style="font-size: inherit;">return</span></span><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0);"> gives the method a value.&nbsp; Notice the Return Type now says <g class="gr_ gr_4 gr-alert gr_spell gr_inline_cards gr_run_anim ContextualSpelling ins-del" id="4" data-gr-id="4">int</g>, which is the data type of the value being returned. &nbsp;</span></p>
</div></div></code></code></pre><pre class="vditor-wysiwyg__preview" data-render="1"><div style="height: auto; width: 935px; left: 13px; top: 70px;" data-block-type="text" class="sl-block" data-block-id="b419ba6b1dcc7d842a4595b8292ea33f"><div style="z-index: 11;" data-placeholder-text="Text" data-placeholder-tag="p" class="sl-block-content" data-gramm_id="20db7505-3458-d317-9382-2a7e13a5d703" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;">
<p>To get to the codes that our method contains we need to call it.Â  To call a class method, you must use the format "<span style="color: rgb(0, 128, 0);">ObjectName.Method()</span><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0);">".Â  In the example below, we call the method with </span><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);">thirdPerson.sayHello();</span></p>

<p>Again we call the method, this time adding it to our string output.&nbsp; The return value will be 1 year added to the age. For our example, we create Jane with age = 45.</p>
</div></div>

<p><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);">int currentYear</span>Â is the parameter needed for the method to run.</p>
</code></div></div><code style="padding-top: 12px; padding-right: 12px; padding-bottom: 12px; padding-left: 12px;">

<section data-id="e0320f9cbb3a5a3ed9c2eec8b4a3631f"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code><code><code style="padding-top: 12px; padding-right: 12px; padding-bottom: 12px; padding-left: 12px;">

</div></div><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code><div data-block-id="31471d433608613924cf78447d343a84" style="min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 451px; height: 195px; left: 15.4998px; top: 115px;" data-block-type="code" class="sl-block"><div style="z-index: 11; border-top-style: solid; border-right-style: solid; border-bottom-style: solid; border-left-style: solid; border-top-width: 1px; border-right-width: 1px; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-left-width: 1px; border-top-left-radius: 5px; border-top-right-radius: 5px; border-bottom-right-radius: 5px; border-bottom-left-radius: 5px; border-top-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-right-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-bottom-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-left-color: rgb(68, 68, 68);" class="sl-block-content notranslate" data-highlight-theme="monokai-sublime"><pre class="java"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;">

<p><span style="color: rgb(0, 0, 0);"><span style="font-size: 0.9em;"><u>Instance variables</u> <strong>name, age, and location</strong> are created in the class, but outside of a method.&nbsp; They are the <strong>attributes</strong> associated with Person. They can be accessed by any method that is a part of the class.</span></span></p>
</div></div>
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 447px; left: 497.5px; top: 394px;" data-block-id="8e25b77ee294b95061483b7ba91eb37d"><div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 14;" data-gramm_id="abed7158-5112-8f02-6ffc-05dab088d4e1" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true">
<p><span style="font-size: 0.9em;"><u>Local variables</u> <strong>birthday</strong>&nbsp;is created inside of methods and therefore can only be accessed by that method. &nbsp;</span></p>
</div></div>
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" style="width: 960px; left: 0px; top: 0px; height: auto;" data-name="text-1d2448" data-block-id="59466e9fa9dee4912dc30d6f40f27649">

<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" data-block-id="98fb78910f9cbb1d6a95bcda20b73fa6" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 126px; left: 43px; top: 265px;"><div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 16;">
<p>instance variable <span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);"><strong>name</strong></span></p>
</div></div>
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 126px; left: 795px; top: 450px;" data-block-id="52a29b4d62c281aa7fdc7cecb4641854"><div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 17;">
<p>local variable <span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);"><strong>name</strong></span></p>
</div></div>
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" data-block-id="e9a16155c2a199d8d3f0171ba642da52" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 897px; left: 32px; top: 118px;"><div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 18;">
<p>In the constructor, you will notice there is a <strong>local variable</strong> <strong><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);">name</span></strong>, just like the <strong>instance variable</strong> <strong><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);">name</span></strong>.&nbsp; How do you call one without it being confused with the other?</p>
</div></div>
<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" style="width: 960px; left: 0px; top: 0px; height: auto;" data-name="text-1d2448" data-block-id="5fe85a5fd79de227f2f6fa737dd39593">
<div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="h1" data-placeholder-text="Title Text" style="z-index: 19;" dir="ui">
<h2>Java OOP Day 2</h2>

<div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="h1" data-placeholder-text="Title Text" style="z-index: 20;" dir="ui">
<h2>Java OOP Day 2</h2>

<p>local variable <span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);"><strong>name</strong></span></p>

<p>In the constructor, you will notice there is a <strong>local variable</strong> <strong><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);">name</span></strong>, just like the <strong>instance variable</strong> <strong><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);">name</span></strong>.Â  How do you call one without it being confused with the other?</p>

<p>Let's spend some time making classes:</p>

<section data-id="a3100772b6fdc6ec0b22d822a9776c72"><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code><code><code style="padding-top: 12px; padding-right: 12px; padding-bottom: 12px; padding-left: 12px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code><div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" data-block-id="99f6290320febb1be5cb4a3d9104bc3d" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 780px; left: 90px; top: 84px;"><div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 10;" data-gramm_id="219635e3-72e5-3d92-7e7c-df8bf908b238" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true">
<p>By convention, attributes (instance variables) are created right after the class declaration and before any methods.&nbsp;</p>

<p>By convention, attributes (instance variables) are created right after the class declaration and before any methods.Â </p>
</code></code></code></code></code></code></div></div><code><code><code style="padding-top: 12px; padding-right: 12px; padding-bottom: 12px; padding-left: 12px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;">
<div style="min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 427px; height: 199px; left: 39px; top: 404px;" data-block-type="code" class="sl-block" data-block-id="36cd3f641e61ae6de06d7acaf8e4db6e"><div style="z-index: 11; border-top-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-top-style: solid; border-top-width: 1px; border-right-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-right-style: solid; border-right-width: 1px; border-bottom-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-bottom-style: solid; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-left-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-left-style: solid; border-left-width: 1px; border-top-left-radius: 5px; border-top-right-radius: 5px; border-bottom-right-radius: 5px; border-bottom-left-radius: 5px; font-size: 106%;" class="sl-block-content notranslate" data-highlight-theme="monokai-sublime"><pre class="java"><code>import java.io.Console;
import java.util.*;</code></pre></div><p data-block="0"><code>public class Book{
   public String author = "Hemmingway";
   public int chapters = 10;</code></p><p data-block="0"><code>  // methods
}</code></p><p data-block="0"><code>    <code data-type="html-inline"></code></code><code data-type="html-inline"></pre></code><code data-type="html-inline"></div></code><code data-type="html-inline"></div></code></code></p><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code><code><div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" data-block-id="eef524c4b14155f401bec880a9fab0ee" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 455px; left: 493px; top: 202px;"><div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 12;" data-gramm_id="720df4da-d430-2558-bcf7-64daa176f788" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true">
<p><span style="font-size: 0.9em;">These variables can only be used in the classes they are declared in. </span></p>

<div style="min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 427px; height: 199px; left: 39px; top: 181px;" data-block-type="code" class="sl-block" data-block-id="1c0e2aed0be4bb9f06d6f419c694eda5"><div style="z-index: 13; border-top-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-top-style: solid; border-top-width: 1px; border-right-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-right-style: solid; border-right-width: 1px; border-bottom-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-bottom-style: solid; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-left-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-left-style: solid; border-left-width: 1px; border-top-left-radius: 5px; border-top-right-radius: 5px; border-bottom-right-radius: 5px; border-bottom-left-radius: 5px; font-size: 106%;" class="sl-block-content notranslate" data-highlight-theme="monokai-sublime"><pre class="java"><code>import java.io.Console;

<p><span style="font-size: 0.9em;">These variables can only be used in the classes they are declared in. </span></p>
</code></div></div><code>
<div style="min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 427px; height: 199px; left: 39px; top: 181px;" data-block-type="code" class="sl-block" data-block-id="1c0e2aed0be4bb9f06d6f419c694eda5"><div style="z-index: 13; border-top-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-top-style: solid; border-top-width: 1px; border-right-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-right-style: solid; border-right-width: 1px; border-bottom-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-bottom-style: solid; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-left-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-left-style: solid; border-left-width: 1px; border-top-left-radius: 5px; border-top-right-radius: 5px; border-bottom-right-radius: 5px; border-bottom-left-radius: 5px; font-size: 106%;" class="sl-block-content notranslate" data-highlight-theme="monokai-sublime"><pre class="java"><code>import java.io.Console;

It is the way in which one class is able to inherit the characteristics (variables and methods) of another class.</p></code></code></code></code></code></code></code></pre><pre class="vditor-wysiwyg__preview" data-render="1"><p style="text-align: left;"><code style="padding-top: 12px; padding-right: 12px; padding-bottom: 12px; padding-left: 12px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code><code>We've mentioned Inheritance before. Â <span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);"><strong>Inheritance</strong></span> is an important part of Object Oriented Programming. It is the way in which one class is able to inherit the characteristics (variables and methods) of another class.</code></code></code></code></code></code></p></pre></div><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code style="padding-top: 12px; <strong>Sub Class:</strong> The class that inherits the other class is known as sub class (or a derived class, extended class, or child class). The subclass can add its own fields and methods in addition to the superclass fields and methods.</p></code></code></code></code></code></code></code></pre><pre class="vditor-wysiwyg__preview" data-render="1"><p style="text-align: left;"><code style="padding-top: 12px; padding-right: 12px; padding-bottom: 12px; padding-left: 12px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code><code><br/>

The subclass can add its own fields and methods in addition to the superclass fields and methods.</code></code></code></code></code></code></p></pre></div><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code style="padding-top: 12px; padding-right: 12px; padding-bottom: 12px; padding-left: 12px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code><code><code><p style="text-align: left;">&nbsp;</p>

<p><span style="font-size: 0.9em;"><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17); text-align: left;">Inheritance supports the concept of âreusabilityâ.&nbsp; W</span><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17); text-align: left;">hen we want to create a new class and there is already a class that includes some of the code that we want, we can </span><span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);"><span style="text-align: left;"><strong>extend</strong></span></span><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17); text-align: left;"> our new class from the existing class. </span></span></p>
</div></div>

<p><span style="font-size: 0.9em;"><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17); text-align: left;">By doing this, we are reusing the fields and methods of the existing class.&nbsp; Remember our Person class?&nbsp; What if we wanted to create a StudentList?&nbsp; Wouldn't they have the same attributes?</span></span></p>

<section data-id="d2826b77987218cd2751bf60b92c33e2"><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code style="padding-top: 12px; padding-right: 12px; padding-bottom: 12px; padding-left: 12px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code><code><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code><div data-block-id="c6cdb1a7db60a72ab0388d9d7b7e170c" style="min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 538px; height: 456px; left: 13.233px; top: 148.164px;" data-block-type="code" class="sl-block"><div style="z-index: 10; border-top-style: solid; border-right-style: solid; border-bottom-style: solid; border-left-style: solid; border-top-width: 1px; border-right-width: 1px; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-left-width: 1px; border-top-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-right-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-bottom-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-left-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-top-left-radius: 5px; border-top-right-radius: 5px; border-bottom-right-radius: 5px; border-bottom-left-radius: 5px; font-size: 85%;" class="sl-block-content notranslate" data-highlight-theme="monokai-sublime"><pre class="java"><code>public class Student extends Person {
   
  //other variables and methods

  public static void main(String[] args) {

    ArrayList&lt;Student&gt; studentList = new ArrayList&lt;Student&gt;();

    Student new_student = new Student();
    new_student.name = "Michael";
    new_student.age = 20;
    new_student.gradYear = 2020;
    studentList.add(new_student);
  
    Student new_student2 = new Student();
    new_student2.name = "Janice";
    new_student2.age = 32;
    new_student2.gradYear = 2019;
    studentList.add(new_student2);
  
    for (Student s : studentList){
      System.out.println("Name: " + s.name + "\nAge: " + 
      s.age +"\nGraduation Year: " + s.gradYear + 
      "\nEnrolled? " + s.enrolled);

<p><span style="font-size: 0.9em;"><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);">Custom class objects can be handily stored in </span><span style="color: rgb(218, 165, 32);">ArrayLists</span><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);">! </span>We can create new instances of the <span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);"><strong>Student</strong></span> object, and then add them into an ArrayList called <span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);"><strong>studentList</strong></span> for storage. We loop through the list using a ForEach loop to output individual objects.</span></p>
</div></div>
<div data-block-id="1b8743b9bb6d34b559238b0ded159916" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 740px; left: 140px; top: 70.164px;" data-block-type="text" class="sl-block"><div style="z-index: 12;" data-placeholder-text="Text" data-placeholder-tag="p" class="sl-block-content" data-gramm_id="6d61eaf2-b495-b453-fc5b-726e829e206d" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true">
<p>How could we use this approach, along with a loop, to create a collection of objects created by the user?</p>

</div></section><section data-id="69cbdbfe01a5bff8de27cc22c75c2e9e"></code></code></code></code></code></code></pre><pre class="vditor-wysiwyg__preview" data-render="1"><div data-block-id="dccf4c2d856a63f1da80ebb7e8140955" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 326px; left: 623px; top: 161.664px;" data-block-type="text" class="sl-block"><div style="z-index: 11;" data-placeholder-text="Text" data-placeholder-tag="p" class="sl-block-content" data-gramm_id="b30e01e3-7fbb-e4bb-129b-919e9eb3a97e" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true" dir="ui"><code style="padding-top: 12px; padding-right: 12px; padding-bottom: 12px; padding-left: 12px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code><code><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;">
<p><span style="font-size: 0.9em;"><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);">Custom class objects can be handily stored in </span><span style="color: rgb(218, 165, 32);">ArrayLists</span><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);">! </span>We can create new instances of the <span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);"><strong>Student</strong></span> object, and then add them into an ArrayList called <span style="color: rgb(255, 0, 0);"><strong>studentList</strong></span> for storage. We loop through the list using a ForEach loop to output individual objects.</span></p>
</code></code></code></code></code></div></div><code style="padding-top: 12px; padding-right: 12px; padding-bottom: 12px; padding-left: 12px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code><code><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;">
<div data-block-id="1b8743b9bb6d34b559238b0ded159916" style="height: auto; min-width: 30px; min-height: 30px; width: 740px; left: 140px; top: 70.164px;" data-block-type="text" class="sl-block"><div style="z-index: 12;" data-placeholder-text="Text" data-placeholder-tag="p" class="sl-block-content" data-gramm_id="6d61eaf2-b495-b453-fc5b-726e829e206d" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true">
<p>How could we use this approach, along with a loop, to create a collection of objects created by the user?</p>
</div></div>

<section data-id="293cef70d11c8e19e0b58610f9ca041c"><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code style="padding-top: 12px; padding-right: 12px; padding-bottom: 12px; padding-left: 12px;"><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code><code><code style="padding-top: 10px; padding-right: 10px; padding-bottom: 10px; padding-left: 10px;"><code><div style="width: 654px; height: 284px; left: 108px; top: 152px;" data-block-type="code" class="sl-block" data-block-id="5871cd21e5956c717c2eebfe8df2b0f4"><div style="z-index: 10; border-top-style: solid; border-right-style: solid; border-bottom-style: solid; border-left-style: solid; border-top-width: 1px; border-right-width: 1px; border-bottom-width: 1px; border-left-width: 1px; border-top-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-right-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-bottom-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-left-color: rgb(68, 68, 68); border-top-left-radius: 5px; border-top-right-radius: 5px; border-bottom-right-radius: 5px; border-bottom-left-radius: 5px; font-size: 83%;" class="sl-block-content notranslate" data-highlight-theme="monokai-sublime"><pre class="java"><code>public class Student extends Person {

<p><span style="font-size: 0.9em;">Next, a <g class="gr_ gr_3 gr-alert gr_spell gr_inline_cards gr_disable_anim_appear ContextualSpelling ins-del" id="3" data-gr-id="3">ForEach</g> loop is used to iterate through the list and output the individual array list objects.</span></p>

<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="text" data-name="text-69fc11" style="height: auto; width: 960px; left: 0px; top: 148px;" data-block-id="456450d9984d4f25eaed6f8a83b95d3d">
<div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 13;" dir="ui">
<p>As you can see, calling System.out.println() on an instance of your class, you'll end up with a weird looking output - and it won't be too useful!</p></div></div></code></pre></div><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code data-line-numbers=""><code><p>&nbsp;</p></code></code></pre><pre class="vditor-wysiwyg__preview" data-render="1"><p><code data-line-numbers="">Â </code></p></pre></div><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code data-line-numbers=""><code><p>This is because the compiler has called toString() on it, which tries to make a readable string out of whatever is given to it.</p></code></code></pre><pre class="vditor-wysiwyg__preview" data-render="1"><p><code data-line-numbers="">This is because the compiler has called toString() on it, which tries to make a readable string out of whatever is given to it.</code></p></pre></div><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code data-line-numbers=""><code><p>&nbsp;</p></code></code></pre><pre class="vditor-wysiwyg__preview" data-render="1"><p><code data-line-numbers="">Â </code></p></pre></div><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code data-line-numbers=""><code><p>We can alter the functionality of toString() by overriding the method for our class.</p>
</div>
<grammarly-extension style="position: absolute; top: 0px; left: 0px; pointer-events: none; z-index: 12;" class="_1KJtL"></grammarly-extension>
</div></section><section data-id="94bfd8d31ea8a2e156766b54ef2efaf9">

<div class="sl-block" data-block-type="code" data-name="code-a3d938" style="width: 672.07px; height: 492.455px; left: 137.465px; top: 110.106px;" data-block-id="bc29819560e4193005a5c7065eee4318"><div class="sl-block-content notranslate" data-highlight-theme="monokai-sublime" data-code-frame="none" style="z-index: 13;"><pre class="java" style="font-size: 16px; line-height: 19px;"><code data-line-numbers="">import java.io.Console;
import java.util.*;</code></pre></div><p data-block="0"><code data-line-numbers="">public class Car {</code></p><p data-block="0"><code data-line-numbers="">	private String name;
	private String color;</code></p><p data-block="0"><code data-line-numbers="">	public Car() {</code></p><p data-block="0"><code data-line-numbers="">	}</code></p><p data-block="0"><code data-line-numbers="">	public Car (String name, String color) {
		this.name = name;
		this.color = color;
	}</code></p><p data-block="0"><code data-line-numbers="">    public String getName(){
		return this.name;
	}</code></p><p data-block="0"><code data-line-numbers="">    public String getColor(){
    	return this.color;
    }</code></p><p data-block="0"><code data-line-numbers="">    @Override
    public String toString()
    {
        return String.format("This %s car is %s.",
                this.getName(),
                this.getColor());
    }</code></p><p data-block="0"><code data-line-numbers="">   public static void main(String[] args){
        Car myCar = new Car("crossover", "blue");</code></p><p data-block="0"><code data-line-numbers="">        System.out.println(myCar); // output: This crossover car is blue.</code></p><p data-block="0"><code data-line-numbers="">   }</code></p><p data-block="0"><code data-line-numbers="">}
<code data-type="html-inline"></code></code><code data-type="html-inline"></pre></code><code data-type="html-inline"></div></code><code data-type="html-inline"></div></code><code data-type="html-inline"></section></code><code data-type="html-inline"><section data-id="60309c1c136f0baed52bff8bfa4d745c"></code></code></p><div class="vditor-wysiwyg__block" data-type="html-block" data-block="0"><pre style="display:none"><code data-line-numbers=""><code><div style="height: auto; width: 960px; left: 0px; top: 102px;" data-block-type="text" class="sl-block" data-block-id="b9a37c051ccab6f5cd35959901d886d4"><div style="z-index: 10;" data-placeholder-text="Text" data-placeholder-tag="p" class="sl-block-content" data-gramm_id="cc91fe87-3e9d-c6d1-b51f-1d3c58b9a732" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true">
<p><strong>Method Overriding</strong></p>
</div></div></code></code></pre><pre class="vditor-wysiwyg__preview" data-render="1"><div style="height: auto; width: 960px; left: 0px; top: 102px;" data-block-type="text" class="sl-block" data-block-id="b9a37c051ccab6f5cd35959901d886d4"><div style="z-index: 10;" data-placeholder-text="Text" data-placeholder-tag="p" class="sl-block-content" data-gramm_id="cc91fe87-3e9d-c6d1-b51f-1d3c58b9a732" data-gramm="true" data-gramm_editor="true"><code data-line-numbers="">

<div class="sl-block-content" data-placeholder-tag="p" data-placeholder-text="Text" style="z-index: 12;" dir="ui"><p style="color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"><span>The </span><span>@Override</span><span> statement is known as an annotation. It should be declared on methods that are overridden. Other than that the method is a normal method implementation. </span></p></div>
